        className: "language-typescript",
        children: "let options: {\n    /**\n     * The URL that the model should be loaded from.\n     * For Teachable Machine, this should be the shareable link that is generated when you export and upload the project.\n     * Can be omitted if both modelJsonUrl and modelMetadataUrl are provided.\n     */\n    modelUrl?: string;\n\n    /**\n     * The URL that the model JSON should be loaded from.\n     * Not required. Can be used if you are storing the model JSON in a custom location (like in a record).\n     */\n    modelJsonUrl?: string;\n\n    /**\n     * The URL that the model metadata should be loaded from.\n     * Not required. Can be used if you are storing the model metadata in a custom location (like in a record).\n     */\n    modelMetadataUrl?: string;\n\n    /**\n     * The camera that should be preferred for the image classifier.\n     * If not provided then the rear (i.e. environment) facing camera will be preferred.\n     */\n    cameraType?: 'rear' | 'front';\n};\n"
      })

      })

(usually 1)\n     * - A number indicates the ratio of frame buffer pixels to output pixels. (e.g. a value of 2 will cause every 2 frame buffer pixels to be correlated with 1 output pixel, meaning that the render resolution is doubled)\n     * - \"recommended\" indicates that CasualOS should try to pick the optimal number.\n     */\n    frameBufferScaleFactor?: number | 'recommended';\n}\n"

      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "Gets the distance that the player bot is from the given dimension."
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "first parameter"
      }), " is the dimension that should be searched for."]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "Possible return values are:"
    }), "\n", _jsxs(PossibleValuesTable, {
      children: [_jsx(PossibleValueCode, {
        value: "-1",
        children: _jsx(_components.p, {
          children: "The player bot cannot access the given dimension."
        })
      }), _jsx(PossibleValueCode, {
        value: "0",
        children: _jsx(_components.p, {
          children: "The player bot is in the given dimension. (dimension tag is true)"
        })
      }), _jsx(PossibleValueCode, {
        value: "1",
        children: _jsx(_components.p, {
          children: "The player bot is viewing the given dimension through a portal. (a portal tag is set to the dimension)"
        })
      })]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.h4, {
      id: "examples-141",
      children: "Examples:"
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.ol, {
      children: ["\n", _jsx(_components.li, {
        children: "Get the distance to the \"fun\" dimension."
      }), "\n"]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.pre, {
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        className: "language-typescript",
        children: "const distance = os.getDimensionalDepth(\"fun\");\nif (distance === 0) {\n    os.toast(\"Player is in the fun dimension\");\n} else if(distance === 1) {\n    os.toast(\"Player is viewing the fun dimension\");\n} else {\n    os.toast(\"Player cannot access the fun dimension\");\n}\n"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.h3, {

        children: "os.raycast(portal, origin, direction)"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "Finds the list of bots that are in the given portal and are intersected by a ray starting at the given origin position and traveling in the given direction.\nReturns a promise that resolves with information about the intersected bots.     }), "\n", _jsx(_components.pre, {

        className: "language-typescript",
        children: "let result: {\n    /**\n     * The list of intersections.\n     */\n    botIntersections: BotIntersection[];\n\n    /**\n     * The ray that the operation sent.\n     */\n    ray: RaycastRay;\n};\n\n/**\n * Defines an interface that represents the intersection of a bot and ray.\n */\nexport interface BotIntersection {\n    /**\n     * The bot that was intersected.\n     */\n    bot: Bot;\n\n    /**\n     * The distance from the origin of the ray that the intersection ocurred at.\n     */\n    distance: number;\n\n    /**\n     * The point that the intersection ocurred at.\n     */\n    point: Vector3;\n\n    /**\n     * The normal that the intersection ocurred at.\n     */\n    normal: Vector3;\n\n    /**\n     * The face that the intersection hit.\n     */\n    face: string;\n\n    /**\n     * The UV coordinates that the intersection ocurred at.\n     */\n    uv: Vector2;\n\n    /**\n     * The portal that the bot is in.\n     */\n    portal: string;\n\n     /**\n      * The dimension that the bot is in.\n      */\n    dimension: string;\n}\n\n/**\n * Defines an interface that represents a ray.\n */\nexport interface RaycastRay {\n    /**\n     * The origin of the ray.\n     */\n    origin: Vector3;\n\n    /**\n     * The direction that the ray travels in.\n     */\n    direction: Vector3;\n}\n"

    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {

    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.pre, {
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        className: "language-typescript",
        children: "let options: {\n    /**\n     * Whether to stream the audio recording.\n     * If streaming is enabled, then @onAudioChunk will be triggered whenever a new \n     * piece of audio is available.\n     */\n    stream?: boolean;\n\n     /**\n      * The MIME type that should be produced. If the given MIME type is not supported, then the default will be used.\n      * Defaults to a containerized format (audio/mp3, audio/webm, etc.) if not specified.\n      */\n    mimeType?: string;\n \n     /**\n      * The number of samples per second (Hz) that audio/x-raw recordings should use.\n      * Defaults to 44100 if not specified.\n      */\n    sampleRate?: number;\n};\n"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["Triggers ", _jsx(TagLink, {
        tag: "@onBeginAudioRecording"
      }), " once recording has started and continuously triggers ", _jsx(TagLink, {
        tag: "@onAudioChunk"
      }), " if ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "stream"
      }), " is set to ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "true"
      }), "."]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.h4, {

      })
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.ol, {
      start: "2",
      children: ["\n", _jsx(_components.li, {
        children: "Stream some raw audio data for 10 seconds."
      }), "\n"]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.pre, {
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        className: "language-typescript",
        children: "await os.beginAudioRecording({\n    stream: true,\n    mimeType: 'audio/x-raw'\n});\n// @onAudioChunk will be called whenever a new sample is available.\nawait os.sleep(10000);\nawait os.endAudioRecording();\n"
      })

        children: "os.endAudioRecording()"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["Stops the audio recording that is in progress.\nReturns a promise that resolves with the recorded data.\nIf the recording was started with ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "stream: true"
      }), ", then the recorded data will be null."]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["Triggers ", _jsx(TagLink, {
        tag: "@onEndAudioRecording"
      }), " once recording has finished."]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.h4, {

    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.ol, {
      children: ["\n", _jsx(_components.li, {
        children: "Record some audio for 10 seconds and download the file."
      }), "\n"]

        children: "os.startFormAnimation(botOrBots, nameOrIndex, options?)"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "Starts the given animation on the given bot or list of bots using the given options.\nReturns a promise that resolves once the animation(s) have been started."
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["Triggers the ", _jsx(TagLink, {
        tag: "@onFormAnimationStarted"
      }), " and ", _jsx(TagLink, {
        tag: "@onAnyFormAnimationStarted"
      }), " listeners once the animation has started."]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "first parameter"
      }), " is the bot or list of bots that the animation should be started on."]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "second parameter"
      }), " is the name of the animation that should be started. Additionally, it can be the index number of the animation that should be played."]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "third paramter"
      }), " is optional and are the options that should be used to play the animation. If provided, it should be an object with the following properties:"]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.pre, {
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        className: "language-typescript",
        children: "let options: {\n    /**\n     * The Unix time in miliseconds that the animation should start at.\n     */\n    startTime?: number;\n\n    /**\n     * The time within the animation clip that the animation should start at in miliseconds.\n     */\n    initialTime?: number;\n\n    /**\n     * The rate at which the animation plays.\n     * 1 means the animation plays normally.\n     * 2 means the animation plays 2x as quickly.\n     * 0 means that the animation is paused.\n     */\n    timeScale?: number;\n\n    /**\n     * The options for looping the animation.\n     * If omitted, then the animation will play once and finish.\n     */\n    loop?: {\n        /**\n         * The looping mode that should be used.\n         */\n        mode: 'repeat' | 'pingPong';\n\n        /**\n         * The number of times that the animation should repeat for.\n         */\n        count: number;\n    };\n\n    /**\n     * Whether the final animation values should be preserved when the animation finishes.\n     */\n    clampWhenFinished?: boolean;\n\n    /**\n     * The number of miliseconds that the animation should take to cross fade from the previous animation.\n     * If null, then this animation takes over immediately. Additionally, if no previous animation was playing then this animation takes over immediately.\n     */\n    crossFadeDuration?: number;\n\n    /**\n     * Whether to warp animation values during a cross fade.\n     */\n    crossFadeWarp?: boolean;\n\n    /**\n     * The number of miliseconds that the animation should take to fade in.\n     * If null, then the animation will not fade in.\n     */\n    fadeDuration?: number;\n\n    /**\n     * The address that the animations should be loaded from.\n     */\n    animationAddress?: string;\n}\n"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.h4, {

Should be an object.\n      * See https://docs.livekit.io/client-sdk-js/interfaces/VideoCaptureOptions.html for a full list of properties.\n      */\n     videoCaptureDefaults?: object;\n \n     /**\n      * The defaults that should be used for uploading audio/video content.\n      * See https://docs.livekit.io/client-sdk-js/interfaces/TrackPublishDefaults.html for a full list of properties.\n      */\n     publishDefaults?: object;\n \n     /**\n      * Whether to enable dynacast.\n      * See https://docs.livekit.io/client-sdk-js/interfaces/RoomOptions.html#dynacast for more info.\n      */\n     dynacast?: boolean;\n \n     /**\n      * Whether to enable adaptive streaming. Alternatively accepts an object with properties from this page: https://docs.livekit.io/client-sdk-js/modules.html#AdaptiveStreamSettings\n      */\n     adaptiveStream?: boolean | object;\n};\n"

      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.h2, {
      id: "debug-actions",
      children: "Debug Actions"
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "Debug actions are actions that are either useful for automated testing/debugging or only available when run inside a debugger."
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.h3, {
      id: "oscreatedebuggeroptions",
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "os.createDebugger(options?)"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "Creates a debug environment that can be used to simulate bots in isolation from the rest of the inst.\nReturns a promise that resolves with an object that contains all of the action functions."
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["One of the special things about debug environments is that the bots in the environment are totally isolated from regular bots.\nThis means that functions like ", _jsx(ActionLink, {
        action: "getBots(..filters)"
      }), " can only access bots that have been created in the debugger\nand actions like ", _jsx(ActionLink, {
        action: "os.toast(message, duration?)"
      }), " don't do anything automatically.\nThis can be useful for automated testing where you want to see what some bots will do without actually letting them do anything."]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["Additionally, debuggers can be configured to be pausable. This allows you to set pause triggers (also known as ", _jsx(_components.a, {
        href: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Breakpoint",
        children: "breakpoints"
      }), ") that temporarily stop the\ndebugger at a specific location in a listener and allows you to inspect the current state of the script.\nPausable debuggers work like normal debuggers, except that some specific functions return promises instead of a result.\nThis is because those functions can trigger user code that could trigger a pause. When this is possible, the debugger returns a promise to your host code so you can properly handle the pause. (See the examples below for more information)"]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "The returned object can be used to create/find bots in the debug environment and simulate interactions.\nThe debug environment also contains several functions that make it easy to observe what has happened inside the environment and therefore determine if everything was performed correctly."
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "first parameter"
      }), " is optional and is the options that should be used to configure the debugger. It is an object and should have the following structure:"]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.pre, {
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        className: "language-typescript",
        children: "let options: {\n    /**\n     * Whether to use real UUIDs for Bot IDs and the uuid() function.\n     * If set to false, then UUIDs will be predictable starting with \"uuid-1\" and continuing up (\"uuid-2\", \"uuid-3\", etc.).\n     * If set to true, then UUIDs will be unpredictable and unique.\n     * Defaults to false.\n     */\n    useRealUUIDs?: boolean;\n\n    /**\n     * Whether to allow scripts to be asynchronous.\n     * If false, then all scripts will be forced to be synchronous.\n     * Defaults to true.\n     * Synchronous scripts are easier to test because they don't rely on back-and-forth (two-way) communication to handle things like web.hook().\n     */\n     allowAsynchronousScripts: boolean;\n\n     /**\n     * The data that the configBot should be created from.\n     * Can be a mod or another bot.\n     */\n    configBot: Bot | BotTags;\n\n    /**\n     * Whether the debugger is pausable.\n     * Pausable debuggers allow you to set pause triggers that temporarily stop the debugger at a specific point in a script\n     * and allow you to inspect the current execution state of the script.\n     */\n    pausable?: boolean;\n};\n"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.h4, {
      id: "examples-198",
      children: "Examples:"
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.pre, {
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        className: "language-typescript",
        metastring: "title='Create a pausable debugger'",
        children: "const debug = await os.createDebugger({\n    pausable: true\n});\n\n// Register a listener that gets called whenever a pause happens in this debugger.\ndebug.onPause(pause => {\n    // Get the current stack frame from the pause\n    const currentFrame = pause.callStack[pause.callStack.length - 1];\n\n    // Set the abc variable to 999\n    currentFrame.setVariableValue('abc', 999);\n\n    // Resume execution after the pause.\n    debug.resume(pause);\n});\n\n// Because the debugger is pausable, the create() function returns a promise\n// because it calls @onCreate which could cause a pause trigger to be hit.\nconst debuggerBot = await debug.create({\n    test: '@let abc = 123; os.toast(abc);'\n});\n\n// Set a pause trigger in the \"test\" script of the bot we just created\n// at line 1 column 16\nconst trigger = debug.setPauseTrigger(debuggerBot, 'test', {\n    lineNumber: 1,\n    columnNumber: 16\n});\n\n// Send a shout. Just like the create() function above, we recieve a promise that we can await.\nawait debug.shout('test');\n\n// Get the resulting actions from the debugger\n// and perform the first one. This should be the os.toast(), but instead of printing 123,\n// it should print 999 because we changed the value of abc during the debugger pause.\nconst actions = debug.getCommonActions();\naction.perform(actions[0]);\n"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.pre, {
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        className: "language-typescript",
        metastring: "title='Create a normal debugger and copy this bot into it.'",
        children: "// Note: variables cannot be named \"debugger\" so we use the name \"debug\" instead.\nconst debug = await os.createDebugger();\nconst debuggerBot = debug.create(thisBot);\n"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.pre, {
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {

      })

        children: "let options: {\n    /**\n     * Gets the tag name mapper that should be used.\n     * This is useful for ensuring that the debugger objects utilize different tag names for the front end.\n     */\n    tagNameMapper?: TagMapper;\n}\n\n/**\n * Defines an interface for a tag mapper.\n */\nexport interface TagMapper {\n    /**\n     * Maps a tag name from its internal name to the name that should be used by the frontend.\n     */\n    forward: (name: string) => string;\n\n    /**\n     * Maps a tag name from its frontend name to the name that is used internally.\n     */\n    reverse: (name: string) => string;\n}\n"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.h4, {
      id: "examples-200",
      children: "Examples:"
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.pre, {
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        className: "language-typescript",
        metastring: "title='Create and attach a debugger'",
        children: "const debug = await os.createDebugger();\n\n// Create a bot in the debugger.\ndebug.create({\n    home: true\n    label: 'Test'\n});\n\n// Attach the debugger to CasualOS.\nawait os.attachDebugger(debug);\n"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.pre, {
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        className: "language-typescript",
        metastring: "title='Attach a debugger with a tag mapper that renames \"home\" tags to \"testHome\"'",
        children: "const debug = await os.createDebugger();\n\n// Create a bot in the debugger.\ndebug.create({\n    home: true\n    label: 'Test'\n});\n\n// Attach the debugger to CasualOS.\n// Because we're providing a tag mapper, the frontend won't see the \"home\" tag in debugger bots,\n// instead it will see \"testHome\" tags.\nawait os.attachDebugger(debug, {\n    tagNameMapper: {\n        forward: (tag) => {\n            if (tag.startsWith('home')) {\n                return `testHome${tag.slice('home'.length)}`;\n            }\n\n            return tag;\n        },\n        reverse: (tag) => {\n            if (tag.startsWith('testHome')) {\n                return tag.slice('testHome'.length);\n            }\n\n            return tag;\n        }\n    }\n});\n"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.h3, {

      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "Registers the given function to be called whenever the debugger is paused by hitting a pause trigger."
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "first argument"
      }), " is the function that should be called when the debugger is paused.\nIt is called with a single argument that represents the current paused state of the debugger:"]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.pre, {
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        className: "language-typescript",
        children: "interface DebuggerPause {\n    /**\n     * The ID of the pause.\n     */\n    pauseId: string | number;\n\n    /**\n     * The pause trigger that started this pause.\n     */\n    trigger: PauseTrigger;\n\n    /**\n     * The state of the pause.\n     * Indicates whether the pause is before or after the node was executed.\n     */\n    state: 'before' | 'after';\n\n    /**\n     * The result of the node evaluation.\n     * Only included for \"after\" pause states.\n     */\n    result?: any;\n\n    /**\n     * The call stack that the debugger currently has.\n     */\n    callStack: DebuggerCallFrame[];\n}\n\n/**\n * Defines an interface that contains information about a single call stack frame.\n */\nexport interface DebuggerCallFrame {\n    /**\n     * The location that was last evaluated in this frame.\n     */\n    location: DebuggerFunctionLocation;\n\n    /**\n     * Gets the list of variables that are avaiable from this frame.\n     */\n    listVariables(): DebuggerVariable[];\n\n    /**\n     * Sets the given variable name to the given value.\n     * @param variableName The name of the variable to set.\n     * @param value The value to set in the variable.\n     */\n    setVariableValue(variableName: string, value: any): void;\n}\n\n/**\n * Defines an interface that represents a location in a debugger.\n */\nexport interface DebuggerFunctionLocation {\n    /**\n     * The name of the function.\n     */\n    name?: string;\n\n    /**\n     * The ID of the bot that this function is defined in.\n     */\n    botId?: string;\n\n    /**\n     * The name of the tag that this function is defined in.\n     */\n    tag?: string;\n\n    /**\n     * The line number that this function is defined at.\n     */\n    lineNumber?: number;\n\n    /**\n     * The column number that this function is defined at.\n     */\n    columnNumber?: number;\n}\n\n/**\n * Defines an interface that represents a debugger variable.\n */\nexport interface DebuggerVariable {\n    /**\n     * The name of the variable.\n     */\n    name: string;\n\n    /**\n     * The value contained by the variable.\n     */\n    value: any;\n\n    /**\n     * The scope that the variable exists in.\n     *\n     * \"block\" indicates that the variable was defined in and exists only in the current block.\n     * \"frame\" indicates that the variable was defined in and exists in the current stack frame.\n     * \"closure\" indicates that the variable was inherited from a parent stack frame.\n     */\n    scope: 'block' | 'frame' | 'closure';\n\n    /**\n     * Whether the variable value can be overwriten.\n     */\n    writable: boolean;\n\n    /**\n     * Whether this variable has been initialized.\n     */\n    initialized?: boolean;\n}\n"
      })

    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.pre, {
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        className: "language-typescript",

      })
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {

Just like the create() function above, we recieve a promise that we can await.\nawait debug.shout('test');\n\n// Get the resulting actions from the debugger\n// and perform the first one. This should be the os.toast(), but instead of printing 123,\n// it should print 999 because we changed the value of abc during the debugger pause.\nconst actions = debug.getCommonActions();\naction.perform(actions[0]);\n"

      children: "Gets the current call stack for the debugger.\nCall stacks are useful for determining program flow and how scripts interact with each other."
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["Only available inside a debugger that was created using ", _jsx(ActionLink, {
        action: "os.createDebugger(options?)"
      }), ".\nAdditionally, this function is only available on pausable debuggers."]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "Returns an array with the following structure:"
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.pre, {
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        className: "language-typescript",
        children: "let callStack: DebuggerCallFrame[];\n\n/**\n * Defines an interface that contains information about a single call stack frame.\n */\ninterface DebuggerCallFrame {\n    /**\n     * The location that was last evaluated in this frame.\n     */\n    location: DebuggerFunctionLocation;\n\n    /**\n     * Gets the list of variables that are avaiable from this frame.\n     */\n    listVariables(): DebuggerVariable[];\n\n    /**\n     * Sets the given variable name to the given value.\n     * @param variableName The name of the variable to set.\n     * @param value The value to set in the variable.\n     */\n    setVariableValue(variableName: string, value: any): void;\n}\n\n/**\n * Defines an interface that represents a location in a debugger.\n */\ninterface DebuggerFunctionLocation {\n    /**\n     * The name of the function.\n     */\n    name?: string;\n\n    /**\n     * The ID of the bot that this function is defined in.\n     */\n    botId?: string;\n\n    /**\n     * The name of the tag that this function is defined in.\n     */\n    tag?: string;\n\n    /**\n     * The line number that this function is defined at.\n     */\n    lineNumber?: number;\n\n    /**\n     * The column number that this function is defined at.\n     */\n    columnNumber?: number;\n}\n\n/**\n * Defines an interface that represents a debugger variable.\n */\ninterface DebuggerVariable {\n    /**\n     * The name of the variable.\n     */\n    name: string;\n\n    /**\n     * The value contained by the variable.\n     */\n    value: any;\n\n    /**\n     * The scope that the variable exists in.\n     *\n     * \"block\" indicates that the variable was defined in and exists only in the current block.\n     * \"frame\" indicates that the variable was defined in and exists in the current stack frame.\n     * \"closure\" indicates that the variable was inherited from a parent stack frame.\n     */\n    scope: 'block' | 'frame' | 'closure';\n\n    /**\n     * Whether the variable value can be overwriten.\n     */\n    writable: boolean;\n\n    /**\n     * Whether this variable has been initialized.\n     */\n    initialized?: boolean;\n}\n"
      })

      id: "mathintersectplaneorigin-direction-planenormal-planeorigin",
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "math.intersectPlane(origin, direction, planeNormal?, planeOrigin?)"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "Calculates the 3D point that a ray starting at the given origin point and traveling in the given direction intersects the grid portal ground plane.\nReturns null if the ray does not intersect the ground plane."
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "Useful for calculating where on the ground something is pointing."
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "first parameter"
      }), " is the 3D point that the ray should start at."]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "second parameter"
      }), " is the direction that the ray is traveling along."]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "third parameter"
      }), " is optional and is the normal vector that the plane should use. For 2D planes, the normal vector is the 3D direction that is perpendicular to the the surface of the plane.\nFor example, a plane that covers the entire XY surface has a normal vector equal to ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "0,0,1"
      }), ", while a plane that covers the YZ surface has a normal vector equal to ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "1,0,0"
      }), ".\nThis parameter defaults to ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "0,0,1"
      }), "."]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "fourth parameter"
      }), " is optional and is the 3D position that the center of the plane should travel through. Defaults to ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "0,0,0"
      }), "."]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.h4, {
      id: "examples-233",
      children: "Examples:"
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.ol, {
      children: ["\n", _jsx(_components.li, {
        children: "Get the spot on the ground that a pointer is pointing at."
      }), "\n"]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.pre, {
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        className: "language-typescript",
        children: "const pointerPosition = os.getPointerPosition('mouse');\nconst pointerRotation = os.getPointerRotation('mouse');\nconst pointerDirection = math.getForwardDirection(pointerRotation);\nconst groundPoint = math.intersectPlane(pointerPosition, pointerDirection);\nos.toast(groundPoint);\n"
      })

    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["Because ", _jsx(_components.a, {

      }), " have limited precision, some calculations cannot be represented\nlike they can in normal math. For example, ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "1/3"
      }), " is ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "0.3333..."
      }), " but in JavaScript ", _jsx(_components.code, {

      }), " gives ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "0.33333333333333331483"
      }), ".\nThis inaccuracy can cause problems when many calculations are done, which can cause numbers that appear to be the same to actually be different."]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The solution is to check the difference between two numbers to see if it is below some arbitrary threshold. In this case, the threshold is ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "0.005"
      }), "."]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "first parameter"
      }), " is the first number that should be checked."]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "second parameter"
      }), " is the second number that should be checked."]

      id: "crypto-actions",
      children: "Crypto Actions"
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.h3, {
      id: "cryptohashalgorithm-format-data",
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "crypto.hash(algorithm, format, ...data)"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["Calculates the ", _jsx(_components.a, {
        href: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cryptographic_hash_function",
        children: "hash"
      }), " of the given data using the specified algorithm and returns the result in the specified format.\nReturns a ", _jsx(_components.a, {
        href: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hexadecimal",
        children: "hexadecimal"
      }), " string, ", _jsx(_components.a, {
        href: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Base64",
        children: "Base64"
      }), " string, or ", _jsx(_components.a, {
        href: "https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Global_Objects/Uint8Array",
        children: "Uint8Array"
      }), " based on the specified format."]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "Hashes are generally useful for validating that a piece of data did not change or for checking to see if two values are the same thing."
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "Supports calculating hashes of strings, numbers, booleans, objects, arrays, and bots."
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "first parameter"
      }), " is a string indicating which algorithm should be used for calculating the hash. The following algorithms are supported:"]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.ul, {
      children: ["\n", _jsxs(_components.li, {
        children: [_jsx(_components.code, {
          children: "sha256"
        }), " (equivalent to ", _jsx(ActionLink, {
          action: "crypto.sha256(...data)"
        }), ")"]
      }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.li, {
        children: [_jsx(_components.code, {
          children: "sha512"
        }), " (equivalent to ", _jsx(ActionLink, {
          action: "crypto.sha512(...data)"
        }), ")"]
      }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.li, {
        children: [_jsx(_components.code, {
          children: "sha1"
        }), " (not recommended unless needed for compatability with external software)"]
      }), "\n"]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "second parameter"
      }), " is a string indicating which format the hash should be output as. The following formats are supported:"]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.ul, {
      children: ["\n", _jsxs(_components.li, {
        children: [_jsx(_components.code, {
          children: "hex"
        }), " - The output should be a hexadecimal string."]
      }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.li, {
        children: [_jsx(_components.code, {
          children: "base64"
        }), " - The output should be a Base64 string."]
      }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.li, {
        children: [_jsx(_components.code, {
          children: "raw"
        }), " - The output should be a ", _jsx(_components.a, {
          href: "https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/JavaScript/Reference/Global_Objects/Uint8Array",
          children: "Uint8Array"
        }), "."]
      }), "\n"]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "other parameters"
      }), " are the pieces of data that should be included in the hash. If multiple pieces of data are included, they will be concatenated."]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.h4, {
      id: "examples-244",
      children: "Examples"
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.pre, {
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        className: "language-typescript",
        metastring: "title='Calculate the SHA-256 hex hash of a string'",
        children: "const hash = crypto.hash(\"sha256\", \"hex\", \"hello, world\");\nos.toast(hash);\n"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.pre, {
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        className: "language-typescript",
        metastring: "title='Calculate the SHA-256 base64 hash of a string'",
        children: "const hash = crypto.hash(\"sha256\", \"base64\", \"hello, world\");\nos.toast(hash);\n"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.pre, {
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        className: "language-typescript",
        metastring: "title='Calculate the SHA-256 raw hash of a string'",
        children: "const hash = crypto.hash(\"sha256\", \"raw\", \"hello, world\");\nconsole.log(hash);\n"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.pre, {
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        className: "language-typescript",
        metastring: "title='Calculate the SHA-512 hex hash of a string'",
        children: "const hash = crypto.hash(\"sha512\", \"hex\", \"hello, world\");\nos.toast(hash);\n"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.pre, {
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        className: "language-typescript",
        metastring: "title='Calculate the SHA-1 hex hash of a string'",
        children: "const hash = crypto.hash(\"sha1\", \"hex\", \"hello, world\");\nos.toast(hash);\n"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.h3, {
      id: "cryptosha256data",
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "crypto.sha256(...data)"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["Calculates the ", _jsx(_components.a, {
        href: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SHA-2",
        children: "SHA-256"
      }), " ", _jsx(_components.a, {
        href: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cryptographic_hash_function",
        children: "hash"
      }), " of the given data.\nReturns a ", _jsx(_components.a, {
        href: "https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hexadecimal",
        children: "hexadecimal"
      }), " string that represents the computed hash."]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "Hashes are generally useful for validating that a piece of data did not change or for checking to see if two values are the same thing."
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "Supports calculating hashes of strings, numbers, booleans, objects, arrays, and bots."
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: [_jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "Each parameter"
      }), " is a piece of data that should be included in the hash. If multiple pieces of data are included, they will be concatenated."]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.h4, {
      id: "examples-245",
      children: "Examples"
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.ol, {
      children: ["\n", _jsx(_components.li, {
        children: "Calculate the hash of a string."
      }), "\n"]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.pre, {
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        className: "language-typescript",
        children: "const hash = crypto.sha256(\"hello, world\");\nos.toast(hash);\n"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.ol, {
      start: "2",
      children: ["\n", _jsx(_components.li, {
        children: "Calculate the hash of an object."
      }), "\n"]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.pre, {
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        className: "language-typescript",
        children: "const hash = crypto.sha256({\n    abc: \"def\"\n});\nos.toast(hash);\n"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.h3, {
      id: "cryptosha512data",
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "crypto.sha512(...data)"
      })

        children: "reliable"
      }), " (the encrypted data cannot be changed without making it unreadable), and ", _jsx(_components.em, {

    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {

      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "crypt.sign(keypair, secret, data)"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "Calculates the digital signature for the given data using the given keypair and secret (also commonly known as a password)."
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["Use ", _jsx(ActionLink, {
        action: "crypto.keypair(secret)"
      }), " to create a keypair that can be used to create signatures."]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["Use ", _jsx(ActionLink, {
        action: "crypto.verify(keypair, signature, data)"
      }), " to validate signatures."]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "Digital signatures are used to verifying the authenticity and integrity of data."
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "This works by leveraging asymmetric encryption but in reverse."
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "If we can encrypt some data such that only the public key of a keypair can decrypt it, then we can prove that\nthe data was encrypted (i.e. signed) by the corresponding private key."
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "And since the public key is available to everyone but the private\nkey is only usable when you have the secret, we can use this to prove that a particular piece of data was signed by whoever knows the secret."
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "Note that because of how digital signatures work, signing the same data with the same keypair will produce the same signature."
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "first parameter"
      }), " is the keypair that should be used to sign the data."]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "second parameter"
      }), " is the secret that was used to encrypt the private key of the keypair."]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "third parameter"
      }), " is the string data that should be signed."]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.h4, {
      id: "examples-254",
      children: "Examples:"
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.ol, {
      children: ["\n", _jsxs(_components.li, {
        children: ["Create a signature for the string ", _jsx(_components.code, {
          children: "\"hello\""
        }), "."]
      }), "\n"]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.pre, {
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        className: "language-typescript",
        children: "// Returned from crypto.keypair()\nconst keypair = \"vK1.ugqz8HzhaQhfORc8Coc6WVHTciMrcmfSUuw99KLRJYk=.djEuak1QNkF5MHFzMTBFMXRHamR1ZFhqTmRTV3AycjVyZUsudzFjSWZWVUFQVUdqK3hTM000NUduYUlNQ094SUhCTUEuanYrZEQwNVJFVGo3UzRPSklQQUkxc3U0anZjUmxrTEM2OW1BajkyMkxxdTFZd2sxNzV5QW9Dc3gwU3RENlQ0cmtNTVk4b2Zna2JRVTIrQmp5OUIrTTJsaFI2ajcyb0lJdmdSWkRXRU9lZE09\";\n\nconst signature = crypto.sign(keypair, \"my secret\", \"hello\");\nos.toast(signature);\n"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.h3, {
      id: "cryptoverifykeypair-signature-data",
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "crypto.verify(keypair, signature, data)"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "Validates that the given signature was created by the given keypair for the given data.\nReturns true if the signature is valid. Returns false otherwise."
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {

    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {

      children: "Certificates are useful for creating signatures for tag values that CasualOS is aware of and will validate for you."
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["Certificates are similar to keypairs except that they themselves are signed by another certificate.\nThis creates a ", _jsx(_components.a, {

        children: "chain of trust"
      }), " that can be used to establish the validity of any arbitrary certificate.\nThe certificate that created the signature is called the \"signing/signer certificate\" and the certificate that recieved the signature is called the \"signee certificate\"."]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "Each certificate contains the following information:"
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.ul, {
      children: ["\n", _jsx(_components.li, {

      }), "\n", _jsx(_components.li, {
        children: "A signature from the signing certificate."
      }), "\n"]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "In CasualOS, there are two types of certificates:"
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.ol, {
      children: ["\n", _jsx(_components.li, {
        children: "Root certificates."
      }), "\n", _jsx(_components.li, {
        children: "Non-root certificates."
      }), "\n"]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: [_jsx(_components.em, {
        children: "Root certificates"
      }), " are certificates that are both signee and signer. This means that the certificate used its own keypair to create the signature.\nAs such, the validity of the certificate cannot be checked apart from simply trusting it. Only one root certificate is allowed per inst on a first-come first-serve basis.\nOnce a root certificate is created for a inst, another cannot be created."]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: [_jsx(_components.em, {
        children: "Non-root certificates"
      }), " are certificates that are signed by another certificate. This means that another certificate's keypair was used to create the signature.\nAs such, the validity of the certificate can be checked by following the chain of trust back to the root certificate.\nIf the chain does not end at the root certificate for the inst, then the certificate is invalid and any signatures created by it will also be invalid."]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["Use ", _jsx(ActionLink, {
        action: "crypto.keypair(secret)"
      }), " to create a keypair that can be used to create signatures."]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["Use ", _jsx(ActionLink, {
        action: "crypto.signTag(certificate, secret, bot, tag)"
      }), " to create signatures for a certificate."]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "first parameter"
      }), " is the certified bot that should be used to sign the new certificate. If given null, then the new bot will be self-signed."]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {

      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.h3, {

    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {

    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["Use ", _jsx(ActionLink, {

      id: "examples-262",

      children: ["\n", _jsxs(_components.li, {

          children: "@onClick"
        }), " script is signed."]
      }), "\n"]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.pre, {
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        className: "language-typescript",
        children: "const valid = crypto.verifyTag(bot, 'onClick');\n\nif (valid) {\n    os.toast('onClick is valid!');\n} else {\n    os.toast('onClick is not valid.');\n}\n"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.h3, {
      id: "cryptorevokecertificatecertificate-secret-signer",
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "crypto.revokeCertificate(certificate, secret, signer?)"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "Revokes the given certificate and any signatures that it has created.\nIn effect, this deletes the certificate bot from the inst.\nAdditionally, any tags signed with the given certificate will no longer be verified."
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "Returns a promise that resolves when the certificate has been revoked."
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "Revoking a certificate works by creating another record (called a revocation) that is signed by either the original certificate\nor an ancestor of the original certificate. This record is then stored in the shared space and lets everyone see that the certificate is no longer valid."
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "first parameter"
      }), " is the certificate that should be revoked."]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "second parameter"
      }), " is the secret that should be used to decrypt the corresponding certificate's private key.\nIf the signer parameter is specified, then this is the secret for the signer certificate.\nIf the signer parameter is omitted, then this is the secret for the certificate that is being revoked."]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "third parameter"
      }), " is optional and is the certificate that should be used to perform the revocation process.\nIf not specified, then the revocation will be signed by the revoked certificate (self-signed revocation).\nIf specified, then the revocation will be signed using the given certificate.\nNote that any certificate that is specified must either be the original certificate or an ancestor of the original certificate."]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.h4, {
      id: "examples-264",
      children: "Examples:"
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.ol, {
      children: ["\n", _jsx(_components.li, {
        children: "Revoke a certificate with itself."
      }), "\n"]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.pre, {
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        className: "language-typescript",
        children: "const cert = getBot('id', certificateId);\nawait crypto.revokeCertificate(cert, 'secretForCert');\n\nos.toast('Certificate revoked!');\n"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.ol, {
      start: "2",
      children: ["\n", _jsx(_components.li, {
        children: "Revoke a certificate using another certificate."
      }), "\n"]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.pre, {
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        className: "language-typescript",
        children: "const certToRevoke = getBot('id', certToRevokeId);\nconst signingCert = getBot('id', signingCertId);\n\nawait crypto.revokeCertificate(certToRevoke, 'secretForSigningCert', signingCert);\n\nos.toast('Certificate revoked!');\n"
      })

    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {

    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "Apps work by utilizing a subset of HTML that works in the CasualOS middle-end and can be synced to the CasualOS front-end. This allows\napps to leverage all the power of bots, tags, and tag masks while at the same time being able to seamlessly integrate with the front-end."
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.h3, {
      id: "osregisterappappid-bot",

      children: "Registers a app with the given ID, bot, and options. Returns a promise that resolves when the app has been registered.\nCan be called multiple times with new options to override previous options."
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["Once setup, CasualOS will send a ", _jsx(TagLink, {

        action: "os.compileApp(appId, content)"
      }), " to set what the app displays."]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {

      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {

    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {

        action: "os.compileApp(appId, content)"
      }), "."]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {

        action: "os.compileApp(appId, content)"
      }), " with the HTML you want the app to show.\nSince JavaScript does not natively support HTML, we are using a special extension called ", _jsx(_components.a, {
        href: "https://reactjs.org/docs/introducing-jsx.html",
        children: "JSX"
      }), " that adds HTML-like syntax to JavaScript.\nAt the most basic, JSX is like writing HTML inside JavaScript:"]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.pre, {
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {

    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {

      })]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["CasualOS also includes a helper called ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "html"

    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.pre, {

        children: "const { useState, useCallback } = os.appHooks;\n\nfunction Counter() {\n    const [value, setValue] = useState(0);\n    const increment = useCallback(() => {\n        setValue(value + 1)\n    }, [value]);\n\n    return (\n        <div>\n            Counter: {value}\n            <button onClick={increment}>Increment</button>\n        </div>\n    );\n}\n\nawait os.registerApp('myapp', thisBot);\nawait os.compileApp('myapp', <Counter/>);\n"

    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["Specifies that the given prefix should be used to indicate that the tag contains script content.\nUse this function to specify custom prefixes that function similarly to ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "@"
      }), " or ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: ""
      }), "."]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "first parameter"
      }), " is the prefix that should indicate that the rest of the tag value is a script."]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "second parameter"
      }), " is optional and is the options that should be used for the prefix. It is an object and should have the following structure:"]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.pre, {
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        className: "language-typescript",
        children: "let options: {\n\n    /**\n     * The language that scripts with the prefix should be interpreted as.\n     * \n     * \"javascript\" and \"typescript\" can be used for general purpose programming.\n     * \n     * \"jsx\" and \"tsx\" are extensions to JavaScript and TypeScript which includes the ability\n     * to write HTML-like code that gets converted to JavaScript/TypeScript code.\n     * \n     * \"json\" can be used to interpret the data as JSON (like ).\n     * \n     * \"text\" can be used to interpret the data as plain text.\n     * \n     * Defaults to \"javascript\".\n     */\n    language?: \"javascript\" | \"typescript\" | \"json\" | \"jsx\" | \"tsx\" | \"text\";\n    \n    /**\n     * The name of the prefix.\n     */\n    name?: string;\n};\n"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.h4, {
      id: "examples-274",
      children: "Examples:"
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.ol, {
      children: ["\n", _jsxs(_components.li, {

        }), " as an script prefix."]

    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.ol, {

      children: _jsx(_components.code, {

      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.h3, {
      id: "experimentlocalpositiontweenbot-dimension-position-easing",
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "experiment.localPositionTween(bot, dimension, position, easing?)"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "Locally plays a tween that moves the given bot in the given dimension to the given position.\nOptionally allows customizing the easing of the tween."
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "Returns a promise that resolves when the tween is finished."
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "While the tween is playing, any updates to the bot's position and rotation are ignored.\nOnce the tween is done playing, any change to the bot will reset the position/rotation."
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "first parameter"
      }), " is the bot or ID of the bot that should be tweened."]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "second parameter"
      }), " is the dimension that the bot should be tweened in.\nNote that the tween will only work if the given dimension is currently in the grid portal or miniGridPortal."]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "third parameter"
      }), " is the position that the bot should be tweened to. If you exclude a dimension (like ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "x"
      }), ", ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "y"
      }), ", or ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "z"
      }), "), then it will remain unchanged."]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "fourth parameter"
      }), " is optional and is the options that should be used.\nIt is an object with the following properties:"]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.pre, {
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        className: "language-typescript",
        children: "let options: {\n\n    /**\n     * The amount of time that the tween takes to complete in seconds.\n     * The maximum duration is 24 hours (86,400 seconds).\n     * The minimum duration is 0.\n     * Defaults to 1 if not specified.\n     */\n    duration?: number;\n\n    /**\n     * The options for easing.\n     * Defaults to \"linear\" \"inout\" if not specified.\n     */\n    easing?: {\n        /**\n         * The type of easing.\n        */\n        type: 'linear'\n            | 'quadratic'\n            | 'cubic'\n            | 'quartic'\n            | 'quintic'\n            | 'sinusoidal'\n            | 'exponential'\n            | 'circular'\n            | 'elastic';\n\n        /**\n         * Whether to apply the easing at the\n         * start (in), end (out), or start and end (inout) of the tween.\n         */\n        mode: 'in' | 'out' | 'inout';\n    }\n};\n"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.h4, {
      id: "examples-276",
      children: "Examples:"
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.ol, {
      children: ["\n", _jsxs(_components.li, {
        children: ["Tween the bot to X = 10 in the ", _jsx(_components.code, {
          children: "home"
        }), " dimension."]
      }), "\n"]

      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "Locally plays a tween that rotates the given bot in the given dimension to the given rotation.\nOptionally allows customizing the easing of the tween."
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "Returns a promise that resolves when the tween is finished."
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "While the tween is playing, any updates to the bot's position and rotation are ignored.\nOnce the tween is done playing, any change to the bot will reset the position/rotation."
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "first parameter"
      }), " is the bot or ID of the bot that should be tweened."]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "second parameter"
      }), " is the dimension that the bot should be tweened in.\nNote that the tween will only work if the given dimension is currently in the grid portal or miniGridPortal."]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "third parameter"
      }), " is the rotation that the bot should be tweened to in radians. If you exclude a dimension (like ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "x"
      }), ", ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "y"
      }), ", or ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "z"
      }), "), then it will remain unchanged."]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "fourth parameter"
      }), " is optional and is the options that should be used.\nIt is an object with the following properties:"]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.pre, {
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        className: "language-typescript",
        children: "let options: {\n\n    /**\n     * The amount of time that the tween takes to complete in seconds.\n     * The maximum duration is 24 hours (86,400 seconds).\n     * The minimum duration is 0.\n     * Defaults to 1.\n     */\n    duration?: number;\n\n    /**\n     * The options for easing.\n     * Defaults to \"linear\" \"inout\" if not specified.\n     */\n    easing?: {\n        /**\n         * The type of easing.\n        */\n        type: 'linear'\n            | 'quadratic'\n            | 'cubic'\n            | 'quartic'\n            | 'quintic'\n            | 'sinusoidal'\n            | 'exponential'\n            | 'circular'\n            | 'elastic';\n\n        /**\n         * Whether to apply the easing at the\n         * start (in), end (out), or start and end (inout) of the tween.\n         */\n        mode: 'in' | 'out' | 'inout';\n    }\n};\n"

        children: "false"
      }), ".\n", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "mapping"
      }), " can be either ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "gpio"
      }), " or ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "physical"
      }), ".\n", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "mock"
      }), " can be any of ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "raspi-b-r1"
      }), " or ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "raspi-a"
      }), " or ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "raspi-b"
      }), " or ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "raspi-a+"
      }), " or ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "raspi-b+"
      }), " or ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "raspi-2"
      }), " or ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "raspi-3"
      }), " or ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "raspi-zero"
      }), " or ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "raspi-zero-w"
      }), ".\n", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "close_on_exit"
      }), " can be ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "true"
      }), " or ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "false"
      }), ". It is recommended to always be ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "true"
      }), "."]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.h4, {
      id: "examples-287",
      children: "Examples:"
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.ol, {
      children: ["\n", _jsx(_components.li, {
        children: "Initialize rpio with the default options explicitly stated."
      }), "\n"]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.pre, {
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        className: "language-typescript",
        children: "let options = {\n        gpiomem: true,          /* Use /dev/gpiomem */\n        mapping: 'physical',    /* Use the P1-P40 numbering scheme */\n        mock: undefined,        /* Emulate specific hardware in mock mode */\n        close_on_exit: true,    /* On node process exit automatically close rpio */\n}\n\nserver.rpioInit(options);\n"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.h3, {

        children: "server.rpioExit()"

      }), " has been configured to perform events in ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "device"

      })
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["Watch ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "pin"
      }), " for changes and execute the callback ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "cb()"
      }), " on events.\nTo stop watching for ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "pin"
      }), " changes, call ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: ".rpioPoll()"
      }), " again, setting the callback to ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "null"
      }), " (or anything else which isn't a function).\nThe action is only executed if ", _jsx(TagLink, {
        tag: "@onAnyAction"
      }), " has been configured to perform events in ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "device"
      }), " actions."]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "Returns a promise that resolves when"

      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {

    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "second parameter"
      }), " is the callback executed on events."]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "third parameter"
      }), " is 'POLL_LOW', 'POLL_HIGH' or 'POLL_BOTH' and can be optionally used to watch for specific events."]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.h4, {
      id: "examples-298",
      children: "Examples:"
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.ol, {
      children: ["\n", _jsx(_components.li, {
        children: "Poll pin 15 forever, and poll pin 16 to stop all polling."
      }), "\n"]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.pre, {
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        className: "language-typescript",
        children: "function nuke_button(pin) {\n        console.log('Nuke button on pin %d pressed', pin);\n        /* No need to nuke more than once. */\n        server.rpioPoll(pin, null);\n}\n \nfunction regular_button(pin) {\n        /* Watch pin 15 forever. */\n        console.log('Button event on pin %d, is now %d', pin, server.rpioRead(pin));\n}\n \n/*\n * Pin 15 watches for both high and low transitions.  Pin 16 only watches for\n * high transitions (e.g. the nuke button is pushed).\n */\nserver.rpioPoll(15, regular_button);\nserver.rpioPoll(16, nuke_button, 'POLL_HIGH');\n"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.h3, {
      id: "serverrpioclosepin-options",
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "server.rpioClose(pin, options)"

      }), " is a friendly device name.\nThe ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "second parameter"
      }), " is a string with the path to the device.\nThe ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "third parameter"
      }), " is an object with the options you want to connect to the device with.\n", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "{boolean}"
      }), " [autoOpen=true] Automatically opens the port on ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "nextTick"
      }), ".\n", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "{number}"
      }), " [baudRate=9600] The baud rate of the port to be opened. This should match one of the commonly available baud rates, such as 110, 300, 1200, 2400, 4800, 9600, 14400, 19200, 38400, 57600, or 115200. Custom rates are supported best effort per platform. The device connected to the serial port is not guaranteed to support the requested baud rate, even if the port itself supports that baud rate.\n", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "{number}"
      }), " [dataBits=8] Must be one of these: 8, 7, 6, or 5.\n", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "{number}"
      }), " [highWaterMark=65536] The size of the read and write buffers defaults to 64k.\n", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "{boolean}"
      }), " [lock=true] Prevent other processes from opening the port. Windows does not currently support ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "false"
      }), ".\n", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "{number}"
      }), " [stopBits=1] Must be one of these: 1 or 2.\n", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "{string}"
      }), " [parity=none] Must be one of these: 'none', 'even', 'mark', 'odd', 'space'.\n", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "{boolean}"
      }), " [rtscts=false] flow control setting\n", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "{boolean}"
      }), " [xon=false] flow control setting\n", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "{boolean}"
      }), " [xoff=false] flow control setting\n", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "{boolean}"
      }), " [xany=false] flow control setting\n", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "{object}"
      }), " bindingOptions sets binding-specific options\n", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "{Binding}"
      }), " Binding The hardware access binding. ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "Bindings"
      }), " are how Node-Serialport talks to the underlying system. Will default to the static property ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "Serialport.Binding"
      }), ".\n", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "{number}"
      }), " [bindingOptions.vmin=1] see ", _jsx(_components.a, {

          children: "man termios"

      children: "Returns a promise that resolves when the history bots are loaded."
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.h4, {
      id: "examples-329",
      children: "Examples:"
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.ol, {
      children: ["\n", _jsxs(_components.li, {
        children: ["Load the ", _jsx(_components.code, {
          children: "history"
        }), " space."]
      }), "\n"]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.pre, {
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        className: "language-typescript",
        children: "await server.browseHistory();\n"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.h3, {
      id: "servermarkhistoryoptions",
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "server.markHistory(options)"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["Marks the current state as a save point in history. This save point can be restored by using the ", _jsx(ActionLink, {
        action: "server.restoreHistoryMark(mark)"
      }), " action.\nNote that this only saves bots in the ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "shared"
      }), " space. ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "local"
      }), " and ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "tempLocal"
      }), " bots are unaffected."]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "Returns a promise that resolves when the history mark has been created."
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "first parameter"
      }), " are the options that should be used to mark the history point.\nIt should be an object with the following properties:"]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.ul, {
      children: ["\n", _jsxs(_components.li, {
        children: [_jsx(_components.code, {
          children: "message"
        }), " - The message that the new mark should have. Use this as a way to communicate what was special about this save point."]
      }), "\n"]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.h4, {
      id: "examples-330",
      children: "Examples:"
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.ol, {
      children: ["\n", _jsxs(_components.li, {
        children: ["Save the current state of the ", _jsx(_components.code, {
          children: "shared"
        }), " space."]
      }), "\n"]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.pre, {
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        className: "language-typescript",
        children: "await server.markHistory({\n    message: 'First Version of my AUX'\n});\n"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.h3, {
      id: "serverrestorehistorymarkmark",
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "server.restoreHistoryMark(mark)"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "Restores the current state to the state that was saved by the given mark.\nThis will create a new mark with any unsaved changes and another mark with the state that was saved by the given mark."
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "Returns a promise that resolves when the history mark has been restored."
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "first parameter"
      }), " is the bot or bot ID of the mark that should be restored. You can find available marks in the current inst by using the ", _jsx(ActionLink, {
        action: "server.browseHistory()"
      }), " action."]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.h4, {
      id: "examples-331",
      children: "Examples:"
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.ol, {
      children: ["\n", _jsx(_components.li, {
        children: "Restore the state to a given mark."
      }), "\n"]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.pre, {
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        className: "language-typescript",
        children: "// Find a random mark that was loaded by server.browseHistory()\nlet mark = getBot(byTag(\"#history\", true));\n\n// Restore the current state to the given mark.\nawait server.restoreHistoryMark(mark);\n"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.h3, {
      id: "serverrestorehistorymarktoinstmark-inst",
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "server.restoreHistoryMarkToInst(mark, inst)"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "Restores the state in the given inst to the state that was saved by the given mark.\nThis will create a new mark with any unsaved changes in the inst and another mark with the state that was saved by the given mark."
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "Returns a promise that resolves when the history mark has been restored."
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "first parameter"
      }), " is the bot or bot ID of the mark that should be restored. You can find available marks in the current inst by using the ", _jsx(ActionLink, {
        action: "server.browseHistory()"
      }), " action."]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "second parameter"
      }), " is the inst that the state should be restored to. If ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "null"
      }), " or an empty string, then the current inst will be restored."]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.h4, {
      id: "examples-332",
      children: "Examples:"
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.ol, {
      children: ["\n", _jsxs(_components.li, {

          children: "test"
        }), " inst to a given mark."]
      }), "\n"]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.pre, {
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        className: "language-typescript",
        children: "// Find a random mark that was loaded by server.browseHistory()\nlet mark = getBot(byTag(\"#history\", true));\n\n// Restore the current state to the given mark.\nawait server.restoreHistoryMarkToInst(mark, \"test\");\n"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.h3, {
      id: "servershellscript",
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "server.shell(script)"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "Executes the given script on the server."
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "first parameter"
      }), " is the shell script that should be executed."]
    }), "\n", _jsx(Alert, {
      type: "info",
      children: _jsxs(_components.p, {
        children: ["By default, shell scripts are disabled on a server.\nTo enable them, you have to write a custom ", _jsx(TagLink, {
          tag: "@onAnyAction"
        }), " listener on the config bot and run an ", _jsx(ActionLink, {
          action: "action.perform(action)"
        }), "."]
      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.h3, {
      id: "serverloadfilepath-options",
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "server.loadFile(path, options?)"
      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "Loads a file from the server at the given path."
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["Note that on a Raspberry PI, all USB storage devices are mapped into the ", _jsx(_components.code, {
        children: "/drives"
      }), " directory based on the port they were plugged into.\nLoading a file from a USB drive is as simple as specifying the file name.\nIf multiple USB drives are plugged in and have files with the same name, then the file from the USB drive in the smallest numbered port is used."]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.p, {
      children: "Returns a promise that resolves with the data in the file."
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "first parameter"
      }), " is the path that the file should be loaded from. This is usually just the full name of the file to load. (name + file extension)"]
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.p, {
      children: ["The ", _jsx(_components.strong, {
        children: "second parameter"
      }), " are the options that should be used for loading the file."]
    }), "\n", _jsx(Alert, {
      type: "info",
      children: _jsxs(_components.p, {
        children: ["By default, loading files is disabled on a server.\nTo enable it, you have to write a custom ", _jsx(TagLink, {
          tag: "@onAnyAction"
        }), " listener on the config bot and run an ", _jsx(ActionLink, {
          action: "action.perform(action)"
        }), "."]
      })
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.h4, {
      id: "examples-333",
      children: "Examples:"
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.ol, {
      children: ["\n", _jsxs(_components.li, {

          children: "@onBookLoaded"
        }), " shout when it is loaded."]
      }), "\n"]
    }), "\n", _jsx(_components.pre, {
      children: _jsx(_components.code, {

      })
    }), "\n", _jsxs(_components.ol, {
      start: "2",
